## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the rate of change of concentration in a chemical reaction, which is a fundamental concept in chemical kinetics. The available variables, time and concentration, suggest that the task is related to the study of reaction rates and their dependence on concentration and time.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant reaction rate)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A (exponential decay of concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (catalyzed reaction rate dependence on concentration)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (A + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (A**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal concentration-response)
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (relationship between reaction rate constant and temperature)
- Integrated rate law: A = c0 / (c1 + c2 * t) (time dependence of concentration)
- Birch-Megan equation: dA_dt = c0 * (A - A_eq) * A**c1 (competitive inhibition kinetics)
- Pseudo-first-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A (first-order reaction rate with small A)
- Elovich equation: dA_dt = c0 * exp(-c1 * A) (surface reaction kinetics with diffusion limitations)
- Particle size distribution: dA_dt = c0 * t**(-c1) (diffusion-controlled particle growth)
- Reaction-diffusion equation: dA_dt = c0 * (A - A_eq) / (c1 + c2 * t) (spatiotemporal dynamics of reaction and diffusion)
- Volmer-Hinkeinstein equation: k = c0 * exp(-c1 / T) (electrochemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood mechanism: dA_dt = c0 * exp(-c1 / T) (catalytic reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Ketridge-Trevani equation: dA_dt = c0 * (1 - A) / (c1 + c2 * t) (enzymatic reaction kinetics with inhibition)
- Einstein-Smoluchowski equation: dA_dt = c0 * (1 - A) * A**c1 (catalytic reaction rate dependence on concentration and temperature)
- Svedberg equation: dA_dt = c0 * t**(-c1) * (A - A_eq) (particle growth and aggregation kinetics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Reaction rate dependence on concentration → Rational fraction A/(A+c1), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x))
- Reaction rate dependence on temperature → Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T), exp(-c1 / T)
- Sigmoidal concentration-response → Hill equation: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (A**c1 + c2)
- Enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation → Michaelis-Menten kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (A + c1)
- Competitive inhibition kinetics → Birch-Megan equation: dA_dt = c0 * (A - A_eq) * A**c1
- Surface reaction kinetics with diffusion limitations → Elovich equation: dA_dt = c0 * exp(-c1 * A)
- Particle growth and aggregation kinetics → Svedberg equation: dA_dt = c0 * t**(-c1) * (A - A_eq)
- Electrochemical reaction rate dependence on temperature → Volmer-Hinkeinstein equation: k = c0 * exp(-c1 / T)
- Catalytic reaction rate dependence on concentration and temperature → Einstein-Smoluchowski equation: dA_dt = c0 * (1 - A) * A**c1
- Time dependence of concentration → Integrated rate law: A = c0 / (c1 + c2 * t)
